Women's World

Feast for Virtuous Widows 285

— Zi Jiu

Following the trend of "restoration of the old ways," first there was the order prohibiting men and women from bathing together...and then there was the slogan of women returning to the home. It is expected that in this antique new China and new era, monuments to chastity may be brought out again by the old and young as a front for promoting old morality and promoting inherent civilization. Sure enough! On the 8th of this month, the "China Daily" had the following record...

Guangzhou News..."Daluo Village, Panyu, is where the Ma, Chen, and Huang surnames live together, each with thousands of descendants, most of whom go out"

"To make a living. Recently, the local gentry, in order to promote old morality and save the declining customs, decided to allocate 3,000 taels of gold from the surplus of the school funds to investigate the widows of the three surnames, regardless of age, who have been observing chastity for more than three years. A colorful shed was built in the Tianhou Temple, and the widows of the three surnames were invited to a joint banquet, called the 'Feast for Virtuous Widows,' which was held on the 10th day of the lunar month, the Xia Yuan Festival. It was found that there were 413 widows among the Chen, Ma, and Huang surnames. The oldest woman, Ma Chen, was eighty years old and had been a widow for fifty-one years, sitting in the first seat. The youngest woman was Chen Huang, who was only twenty-two years old. She had lost her husband at the age of seventeen and sat in the last seat. First, the deputy township head, Chen Zengling, respectfully invited the women to take their seats, and lectured on Confucian classics and the virtuous widows of the previous Qing dynasty who were erected and honored with archways. The women in the banquet listened attentively, very happily. Only in the evening did they take photos and disperse." After finally fighting for the written agreement of legal co-chastity, suddenly such good news came, which made people feel like crying and laughing!

Widowhood chastity, China's past laws || the early years of the Republic of China, there were regulations praising heroines and virtuous women || had been explicitly praised, but in current law, a widow's remarriage is now considered a legal act! Unexpectedly, Guangdong, the source of the revolution, would actually have such a retrogressive and counter-revolutionary good deed! This makes us sigh, "Where is the revolution?" In addition, we also know that in the current social system, the law is really just a written agreement, and the old forces entrenched in the current society are the source of manufacturing man-eating rites and teachings, which can ignore the law and ignore everything.

"Food and sex are human nature" This is the saying of the ancient sages, and the promoters of restoration will certainly not deny it. Women are people, and they also have human nature. May I ask those who cling to the past, how do they answer? At the feast for virtuous widows, there were eighty-year-old women who had been widows for fifty-one years, as well as twenty-two-year-old young women who had been observing chastity for more than five years. Under the shackles of the old rites and teachings, they were spending time against nature, living a sad and painful life. The so-called "moving to listen, extremely happy," is probably just the fantasy in the muddle-headed minds of those senile gentry, or just a forced smile under authority!

Old rites and teachings! Old rites and teachings, this invisible ferocious tiger, how many thousands of sisters have been swallowed and skinned alive in the past! Because the doors were opened, it had slightly disappeared, and now, with the wind of restoration, it is coming back. Women's movement groups, quickly come and put out this flood and ferocious beast!

The Current State of Chinese Working Women 286

— Hu Guanlu

Everyone knows that China is a semi-colonial, semi-feudal country. Chinese working women — specifically, the vast number of women engaged in manual labor — are, of course, partly subject to the oppression of feudal landlords in rural areas. However, the greater part of them lives under the control of factory capital operated by the masters of the colony.

Chinese cities are dominated by capitalist powers, and Chinese villages also exist under the influence of capitalist countries, our colonial masters, not only indirectly but also directly. To understand the lives of Chinese working women today, we must first pay attention to the state of capitalism that directly impacts these women.

The highest stage of capitalist development is marked by its uneven development and contradictions. The characteristics of capitalism in this stage are:

(1) The concentration of capital and production. Banks are transferred from the hands of intermediaries to those of all-powerful monopolists, and the establishment of financial oligarchies greatly increases the speed of "the process of capital concentration and monopoly formation."

(2) The increasing unification of bank capital and industrial capital; banks become the main masters of production, and financial capital occupies a dominant position in the economy and politics.

(3) The export of capital occupies a particularly important position in economic policy. The entire capitalist country becomes a "parasitic" state and a "rentier state"; this country increases the number of rentiers whose sole task is to clip dividend coupons; they neither produce nor distribute, but are merely consumers who enjoy the fruits of labor without working.

(4) Based on the above elements, the nature of capitalism's division of the world is complete. At this time, capitalism has developed to its final stage, the so-called imperialist stage. The last clear indicator of this stage is the manifestation of international monopoly organizations, which is the desire to divide the world and create one's own colonies.

The highest stage of capitalist development is the imperialist stage, which is also a period of general crisis. This period is not an organization or maturation of capitalist contradictions, nor a refuge, but a time of turmoil, panic, and the need to find another way out.

Capitalism has now reached such a stage, with overproduction, financial panic, and aggression against colonies being its manifestations.

Naturally, seeking colonies is the way out for capitalist countries, and seeking larger colonies is their greater way out. China, with its vast land and large population, is the country that best meets their demands. In recent years, the bankruptcy of Chinese villages and the increasing colonization of the lives of ordinary people, the panic of capitalism has been expressed in our invasion in every detail.

However, under this invasion, the most exploited are manual laborers, and the lives of working women are even more unbearable.

Let us now discuss urban and rural working women separately.

Urban working women, apart from a small number who serve as domestic employees, are mostly factory workers — including the unemployed. In capitalist countries, the wages of female and child laborers are generally lower than those of male laborers. This proves that the system of capitalist countries is fundamentally sexist; it sees women as incapable, cheap, or unable to be responsible and independently engage in labor. Their abilities and the trust others have in them can only be compared with those of minors — child laborers. The capitalist system treats non-working women as commodities and working women as young children. In this respect, Chinese working women, who are subject to the current stage of capitalist aggression, are already in a position where they cannot survive.

Let's first look at urban working women. Leaving aside those engaged in personal labor, let's look at the lives of factory women in recent years:

There are many women workers in Shanghai's light industrial factories. Entrepreneurs use the "female workers' wages are lower than male workers'" tactic, and light industrial factories prefer to recruit female workers. The best-paid and relatively easier job in light industrial factories can be considered to be in silk weaving factories. Skilled workers in silk factories, those who weave the best silk, can earn more than forty yuan a month. However, it is not easy for many people to earn such a wage in a factory with hundreds of women workers; moreover, it is not easy for a woman worker to earn such a wage for several months of the year. This is because it is inevitable that any worker will take sick leave during the year; it is also inevitable that they will be punished and have their wages deducted because the machine or raw materials are faulty, thus ruining the silk. No one can completely and consistently earn their ideal wage every month.

The above situation refers to a small number of skilled workers; skilled workers require many conditions: long years of work, good silk weaving, and "youth and strength."

As for the general situation: new workers must pay a deposit of thirty yuan — those who cannot pay are exempt, which is a special and necessary procedure for silk factories — and then enter the factory as apprentices. The apprenticeship period is indefinite; with good opportunities, they can learn earlier; with bad opportunities, it can be extended to more than a year. There is no wage during the apprenticeship period. After learning, they must wait for the factory to assign their own machine. If the factory does not have a spare machine to assign to them at that time, they cannot get the regular wage — the wage for weaving on someone else's machine can only be calculated at a certain percentage.

The life in silk factories is the best life for women workers. Next are cotton mills and silk reeling factories. In cotton mills, there is generally no time for meals; the machines do not stop during meals, and the rice is eaten with cotton wool. The amount of wages is only forty to fifty cents a day.

The situation in silk reeling factories and other factories is similar. With this amount of wages, female workers not only have to support themselves, but also have to take it home to support their parents, children, and unemployed husbands.

Female workers have no rest period before and after childbirth, and all their salaries are deducted for taking leave. Women who live this kind of working life often lose their lifelong health during their young reproductive years!

The capitalist crisis's invasion of China drags formerly unliberated lower-class "slave" women under machines to serve as colonial cows.

The above is the life of urban working women. Now let's look at rural working women:

Also because of the capitalist crisis's attack on us, China's rural economy has fallen into a fragmented state. Of course, farmers who engage in four seasons of cultivation cannot survive by relying on their own production; in addition, landlords who are about to go bankrupt take advantage of them even more intensely to maintain their own comfort. Under these conditions, how do rural working women live?

If the husband sells all his labor and it is not enough to maintain the family's livelihood, the women have to do things that they are unwilling to do and cannot do. Disregarding their physical strength, they work in the fields and mountains; they do not rest during illness, childbirth, and raising children; as women who combine the responsibilities of domestic servants, mothers, wives, and chicken, duck, dog, and pig keepers, and throw themselves into field work, they cannot care about aging, illness, and sacrifice to serve all their masters and maintain their own lives; however, in reality, they sacrifice their future lives to maintain their current lives. Such working women have no leisure and no possibility to take care of their lifelong affairs, their own happiness, their present and future health and well-being. In this semi-feudal country of China, women have never broken the old shackles, especially working-class women, who rely on despised labor and trivial household services; relying on being passive sexual machines, they buy out their unfree lives; however, this kind of life is not the most bitter. The gifts that capitalist intensification has given them in recent years; maintaining their old lives and adding new labor to them, makes working women more prone to disease and death. Chinese working women, if they want to gain liberation and live human lives, the anti-feudal and especially the anti-foreign invasion efforts are absolutely not something that can be relied on others, but their own task!

My Marriage Problem 287

— Hong Hua

The issue of marriage is truly a struggle in my life. With the progress of the times and the gaining of self-awareness, this struggle is almost an epitome of a social mechanism.

When I was still in my mother's womb, I was already predetermined to be someone's property as a gift from my father to tie up friendly relations. The environment gave me confinement and imprisonment, and the demands of sexual love burned like a raging fire; I was like a captive, carried off and subdued in a feudal iron cage. That stranger, the so-called husband, had to satisfy my every arbitrary demand for enjoyment; in his eyes, I was respected like a god; he knew clearly that all social customs and laws, like iron nets through which electric currents passed, were densely layered around our family, and I, the god he kept, had no way to escape. Nothing is more hypocritical and shameful than this system of monogamy, which originates from private property and proclaims the absolute domination of men over women — on the one hand, he used a kind and joyful face to cover up the ferocious inner heart of a beast, confining me to be tamed to relieve his sorrows and unconditionally serve him; on the other hand, he sought his emotional satisfaction without any scruples. — How ridiculous and trivial this is! Finally, I jumped out of this vicious trap.

Free love, originating from the individualistic demand for sexual love, was the path for me, a prisoner liberated from a feudal family. However, this life gave me great displeasure. Although I cannot deny the great significance of representing an independent personality in gender relations, in this embrace of love, my life stagnated and suffocated, as if I were a corpse whose coffin had been closed and a final verdict had been reached; everything had lost its luster to me, and my heart was as dead as ashes. The meaning of my economic independence was to obtain a profession that would make the new (small) family more vibrant. My lover, like me, devoted his whole heart and body to love and was loyal to love. Is love sacred? This is a deceptive statement! "Love," like life itself, demands to be developed, demands new adaptations; it is the creative self. Inevitably, this relationship (hypocritical free love) gave us boredom, depression, and undeniably, mutual harm to our lives. How terrible it is when we routinely have to kiss or have sex, a physiological necessity, a habitual necessity, forcing our love to complete itself, and behind the joy, love shivers with the coldness of having its marrow devalued. I asked myself: "Is love the entire meaning of your life?" In the midst of this, the spur of life, the demands of life, and especially the era-specific critique, I became rational.

I fully understand my life and the sexual love in gender relations, in all the social relationships that do not belong to myself, and what attitude I should take to solve my marriage problem.

Men almost without exception are confined by the atmosphere of feudal remnants. If he is only loved by me for his heroic spirit and magnificent demeanor, then undoubtedly, I will only get the satisfaction of pure sexual desire, and disillusionment will follow our joy. This life of sacred love, stagnating in the individual circle, has given us many lessons, and should marriage not be treated as a child's play, whether in society or in one's own spirit and time? Then shall we let it be trapped in that disillusioned love? If the one I love is a stumbling block on my path forward, then shall we stop and no longer move forward? Kick away this stumbling block? Then how can our long journey bear the burden of this private drag? Singleness? Why kill my physiological nature? Therefore, his understanding of society, his compelling vision of society, his life in society, and mutual understanding and harmony are necessary conditions.

In this union, what people who simply treat love as child's play cannot imagine is how a brand new spirit is displayed in the mutual understanding and criticism, the dialectical development of new forces, and the promotion of the high development of human life. This force makes our tense lives, in both of our hearts, fear that our own lack of effort or laziness will be abandoned by the times and be unfortunate. Because both sides' love is built on the mutual effort of learning and career; this effort is not only the driving force of the mutual attraction of love, but love is precisely the power that accompanies each other's spiritual upward movement to gain new life; therefore, the other party's abandonment is a sign of the depravity of my life, which is the important reason for this unfortunate result; this contains social significance, who dares to risk this taboo and willingly live in the contempt of falling down? Therefore, in our sexual relationship, there is no rigid perfunctoriness or playing with it; whether it is after a long separation or a long period of cohabitation, every embrace, trembling from the source of life, intoxicates us with the love of the first moment. Here, the constant new forces are the chains that bind us tightly together; if love suddenly springs from the heart for someone, we must frankly say to each other the correct criticism: "You are wrong!" Or say: "Indeed, her (or his) points of attraction are worth your love!" We clearly recognize that any means of restraining the other party is a fatal destruction to the spirit and love, that is, one's own destruction. Jealousy originating from possession has gradually been forgotten in our relationship! The positive view and review of life quenched some burning flames in my or his heart, and we became more closely linked.

It is undoubtedly the case that gender relations are created forward with career as the center, so if there are any reasons that cause cracks between us, it is either that I have factors that destroy "love" or that he is degenerate. If this driving force for our spiritual upward movement cannot function, is there still a need to maintain this corrupt relationship? Basically, one is upward and one is declining, it goes without saying that this declining one gives the upward one a terrible obstacle; what will "love" rely on to not die? What is the basis of this relationship? Naturally, there is only separation.

Struggle is life! Gender relations must be developed forward with struggle!

Old Mou 288

— Zi Gang

The winter in the north country is like a knife.

There is no wind, but the cold still urges people to shrink their necks and huddle together like hedgehogs, and everyone has a premonition in their hearts: it will snow soon.

In the evening, after unloading a heavy burden, he shook the dust off his body and wound his way back to his residence along a winding path. The slowly drifting snowflakes hastened people's steps, and the tips of their noses ached.

When I walked past the low wall by the roadside, I was stunned. So many people were surrounding the door, with those in the back squeezing those in the front. Mixed in were the children's shouts, and I smelled the scent of paper money. I understood that someone had just stopped breathing inside.

"Old Mou is really cruel, abandoning three children and only caring about following the children's father to die..."

"It's also for the money! When the head of the family (Note: People in Beiping call their husband 'head of the family.') was alive, he could still supplement the family a little, but now he has to incur a debt!" I recognized that this was the seamstress Lin Dejia's family. She frowned tightly and continued: "Old Mou doesn't know how long she's been hanging. Alas, there's still a pile of laundry she took on waiting to be washed in the basin."

Hearing that it was a laundry woman, I suddenly understood. There wouldn't be many laundry women in this alley. It must be the one who often came to the owner of my house to pick up bedsheets. Sometimes she would ask me, and I would stretch out my strong arms and joke with the woman, saying that I was stronger than her. It was true, this woman's leanness wouldn't make people believe that she could bend over the green pottery basin for five or six hours every day. Only the corners of her eyes showed that she was only in her thirties.

I patted Lin Dejia's shoulder:

"Hey, what's going on, so crowded!"

The woman put down her tiptoed toes, surprised:

"You — you this girl is really scary! Come, come, see Old Mou, punish you, Old Mou's head of the family is still stiff on the kang!"

This time, Lin Dejia used all her strength, and we successfully blocked the doorway. I didn't know if it was really impossible to squeeze in, or if Lin Dejia herself was timid.

People's gaze seemed to shift from the dead man on the kang to the living man sitting on the long bench wiping tears, who almost died too. Ignoring the deep, purplish-red marks on his neck, which was revealed by the open collar, that was the reason why a tall man was swelling with veins on his forehead and scolding. He lived in a taller tiled house in the same alley. Old Mou's rented house was his. At this time, the cursing continued:

"Never heard of it, when the head of the family dies, instead of quickly arranging the funeral, she stubbornly hangs herself. Are we still planning to rent out this house tomorrow!" He wiped his sweat on a snowy day, "The women should also have an idea!"

Three children, all no taller than a table, stared blankly at their dead father on the kang and their sobbing mother. The woman held the smallest one in her arms, and two small eyes stared at the deep, purplish-red marks in her neck, as if with pity and awe.

The woman burst into tears again, pointing to one on the kang:

"I don't even have money to buy a straw mat. His pair of sugar-peddling poles can't even sell for a few dollars. That's how he'll go underground!..."

"You might as well die too, then it'll be over? Thinking about other people's coffins!" The man breathed out, "Think of a way to borrow some money to bury him, and don't rent my house as soon as possible."

Everyone persuaded him, and the man went out angrily. The woman stopped crying and discussed with her companions borrowing ten or so dollars to bury the dead. She would slowly repay the debt by doing more work herself.

People gradually dispersed and came out. Snowflakes had accumulated on the ground and didn't melt, and gloom ruled the world. Stepping out of the door, I could still faintly hear a weak sigh.

"There is no freedom even in death!"

The days flew by. It had been more than ten days since that snowy day. Late at night, when I walked past a group of resting rickshaw pullers, I saw the woman who wanted to die but couldn't. She was busy pouring hot tea for the rickshaw pullers. A carrying pole lay horizontally on the ground, with a basket of rough bowls on one end and a teapot a little smaller than a wine jar on the other.

"Old Mou! My voice leaped with joy."

A thin face lifted up and recognized me after a long time:

"Ah, it turns out it's you!" Then she stopped talking.

I waited for her business to end, and she picked up the load. She counted the gains in the basket, which were nine large coins. In the small alley, two people, strangers yet familiar, walked along. She said that the money was borrowed in advance from the washing clients and would be deducted slowly. Sooner or later, the money from selling hot tea would feed the three children. Her voice was so slow, and the tone suffocated me. A heavy life, having reaped away the laughter, was slowly crawling in the darkness.

When she arrived at her door, she put down the load and slowly used a rusty key to open the rusty lock.

The house was pitch black. The woman shuffled in, carrying the load. In the dimness, I seemed to see the three sleeping faces on the earthen kang. Perhaps when their mother lay down beside them, they wouldn't even stir, because their dreams were so deep and so far away.

Jianchuan Woman 289

— Xin Er

"Better to hire a Jianchuan woman,

Than buy a mule to haul."

This is a saying sung by people near Jianchuan. It is rare indeed that a woman is considered inferior to a mule.

Jianchuan County is in Yunnan, about a hundred miles from Dali. It is also a remote place, and the women there are very different from those in other places. If women in Shanghai eat two bowls of rice per meal, then they must have at least ten bowls. Their feet are said to be like a small steamer, that big. Though this is an exaggeration, it is evident that their natural feet are much bigger than bound feet!

There is no need to detail the height and strength of their bodies with measurements. Ordinarily, it takes at least two people to carry a coffin, but a Jianchuan woman can carry a coffin with one hand. How amazing is that! The many strongmen and heroes in Chinese history must have indeed had such tall statures.

Let's take an example of their daily hard work and being treated like cattle and horses. There is still nine parts of feudal meaning here, and women most like to be the wife of a scholar. Now scholars have been abolished, and going to foreign schools in other big cities is just as glorious. When women marry a scholar, their husbands will certainly not hire or buy a mule to drag themselves and their luggage over high mountains and ridges to go to school; instead, the women will lift their husbands and place them on their shoulders, and the luggage will be hung on their bodies. Whatever a mule can drag, a Jianchuan woman always has the strength to carry. This unbelievable thing exists in this way. It is by no means difficult to carry so much weight on one's body, crossing high mountains and ridges for more than ten days. It is truly like livestock being used as cattle and horses by men. It is not enough to be good and normal cattle and horses! They have two sayings to laugh at women's inferiority:

"Better to hire a mule to haul,

Than marry a Jianchuan woman!"

It is clear that a Jianchuan woman is inferior to a mule.

It is not that Jianchuan women are born slaves, but rather that it is created by the special economic and geographical environment of Jianchuan. And because it is an era in which the remnants of the old society are still spreading, women are regarded as cattle and horses, as slaves, and used like machines, which is still common everywhere, especially in our old and civilized China. This kind of customs and habits often make people feel nauseous.

The strong and tall bodies and the hard-working labor of Jianchuan women are not shame and meanness. On the contrary, it is precisely the correct path for women, and healthy beauty and the ability to labor are what modern women need most. We should not laugh at Jianchuan women's feet that look like a small steamer, but we should pay attention to canceling:

"Better to hire a mule to haul,

Than marry a Jianchuan woman."

Total Number of Female Civil Servants 290

(Year 22)

Telecommunications Special Issue

The Voice of Cinema

Christmas and New Year 291

— Lü Bing

▲ Using the Telephone ▲ Wishing You Prosperity in the New Year

The year is drawing to a close, and in the blink of an eye, Christmas is approaching, and the New Year is about to begin. During this time, social interactions among people are even more cordial than usual: exchanging gifts is one aspect, and sending greeting cards is another; but for those separated by distance, the longing at the year's end is particularly strong. Every festive occasion makes them feel even more sentimental. What can console them? The answer is telegrams.

Telegrams, used to exchange messages and convey feelings between people around Christmas, can be said to be extremely appropriate. I recall that in the past, telegram fees did not differentiate between New Year's greetings and ordinary telegrams. Later, as major commercial ports grew, and more Westerners resided in China, sending telegrams overseas to express sincere New Year's greetings became a quick way to convey their sentiments. Therefore, Christmas and New Year's greeting telegrams became indispensable for those who paid attention to social etiquette.

In fact, New Year's greeting telegrams are just one type of social telegram. Chinese people are enthusiastic about socializing, talking extensively about it. The Ministry of Communications has taken advantage of this and has already made regulations for cheaper social telegrams. Greeting Christmas and the New Year are most important in social interactions, and the prices have also been reduced accordingly. Modern men and women must pay attention to this.

The peak period for New Year's greeting telegrams was after 1921, especially in major commercial ports, where the numbers were highest. At the end of the year, telegraph office staff were exceptionally busy. During the New Year holidays, all sectors indulged in revelry, and the increase in telegram traffic was the highest of the year. The trend of the times led to the establishment of social telegrams, which, regardless, represent a good sign of celebrating peace and unity.

"Peace," "Cooperation," "Unity" and Telecommunications 292

— Zhen

As the Fifth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang is about to open, the Central Government, for the sake of sincere unity, specially sent Sun Ke and Wang Chonghui to the South to discuss national affairs with the Southwest delegates. The result was exceptionally satisfactory, and they decided on the three principles of "peace," "cooperation," and "unity." This means that the opinions between the Central Government and Guangdong and Hong Kong over the past few years have been completely resolved. From now on, they will work together harmoniously and cooperatively. The great foundation of the Party and the country is established from this point. "A word can revive a nation," which is what the trip of Sun and Wang achieved.

The people of the country hope for "peace," "cooperation," and "unity" is extremely widespread. The need for "peace," "cooperation," and "unity" in the transportation industry is particularly urgent. Taking telecommunications as an example, without the above three principles, there can be no talk of reorganization and expansion. Telecommunications is the nervous system of a country. If one place is not peaceful or one province does not cooperate, it will affect the entire plan, and even destroy the original construction. Looking at the times when wars occur, the telecommunications industry is the first to bear the brunt, such as the congestion of military telegrams, the suppression of commercial telegrams, the arbitrary appointment of bureau directors, the exhaustion of telegram funds, the seizure of telegraph lines, the cutting of telegraph poles, and the borrowing of telegraph staff. All kinds of demands and oppressive situations were too numerous to mention during the warlord era. Under the rule of the National Government, this trend has been somewhat suppressed, but due to the extremely close relationship between telecommunications and military affairs, it is inevitable that it will be subject to military control whenever wars occur. This is in terms of telecommunications itself. As for when armies meet, merchants are cut off, markets become ruins, and rural areas go bankrupt, what telecommunications business can be said to exist during this period? Therefore, the indirect losses of war to telecommunications cannot be measured by distance. Since the national crisis, the authorities have adhered to the doctrine of peace and unity, and in domestic policy, they have tolerated each other for the sake of the country. Except for suppressing bandits, they never resort to armed conflict. Therefore, the telecommunications industry has made daily progress in recent years, which is due to the gift of peace. This is also clear.

As for cooperation, it is even more necessary for telecommunications. Because China is vast in territory, densely populated, economically poor, and lacking talent, it is impossible for the central government to build wired, wireless, and telephone networks covering the entire country all at once. The protection of circuits, the assistance of manpower, and the transportation of materials cannot be achieved without the help of local governments and the public. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications has stipulated supervisory regulations for privately-run local telephone services, allowing them to be established and supervised according to law. The Ministry of Communications has also submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to formulate the "Principles for the Ministry of Communications to Entrust Provincial Governments to Operate Long-Distance Telephone Services," allowing them to go their separate ways but achieve the same goal. This embodies the intention of division of labor and cooperation within the overall system. The former is a matter of law and reason, while the latter is a matter of fact. One is to avoid conflicting with the rights and interests stipulated by the central government, and the other is to seek individual development for each province. Therefore, in June of this year, the Ministry of Communications entrusted the Zhejiang Provincial Government to operate long-distance telephone services, and in July, it carried out the connection between the ministry-run long-distance telephone services and the commercially-run local telephone services. These are all expressions of sincere cooperation.

Since they can live in peace and cooperate sincerely, the telecommunications administration itself is gradually entering the right track, and turning to promote political unity is a matter of course. In recent years, the telecommunications administrations of Guangdong, Guangxi, and other provinces have had many differences with the central government due to political relations. Since the telecommunications conference was held, the representatives from Guangdong, Guangxi, and other provinces have understood the central government's telecommunications policy and its intention to cooperate sincerely. Returning and conveying this to the authorities in Guangdong, Guangxi, and other provinces, the opinions on telecommunications administration are becoming more harmonious. International telegram fees can be paid on time, and unified voice has been established in foreign communications. Now, due to the political unification, the telecommunications unification problem will be solved easily.

When the Ministry of Communications held the telecommunications conference, the author once cited the unified spirit and cooperative spirit of the conference to the people of the country. The telecommunications business is an international communication tool, and there must be no disunity or lack of cooperation. Otherwise, it will be ridiculed as "unorganized" and "non-modern country." But unfortunately, if this phenomenon occurs occasionally, it is not the fault of the telecommunications administration itself, but the reflection of the domestic political environment. Now, the Fifth Plenary Session is held in the capital, deciding on major doubts and establishing major plans. Domestic policy must return to unity. Peace can be built, and cooperation can succeed. All businesses are based on this. Is it just telecommunications?

The Reorganization and Development of the Telecommunications Industry 293

— Bao Zhen

Telecommunications is a sharp tool for people to communicate. Because scientific progress is advancing by leaps and bounds, since the invention of wired telegraph and telephone, in less than a few decades, there have been inventions of wireless telegraph and telephone. Now people use electric current to transmit messages. The tools that they use are wired telegraphs and telephones, and wireless telegraphs and telephones. The machinery is becoming more sophisticated, and the equipment is becoming more perfect. The progress of the telecommunications industry in Europe and the United States is really just beginning. Now I will talk about the reorganization and development of my country's telecommunications industry.

㈠ Wired Telegraph Because my country's wired telegraph has been through a lot of troubled times, the lines have often been accidentally destroyed, and the telecommunications economy is very difficult. Therefore, it is very difficult to build for a while, but the wired telegraph has already has a considerable scale. How can we allow it to be destroyed without trying to reorganize it? If you say that because there is wireless electricity, wired electricity should be eliminated by natural selection, and it can be completely abandoned, that is unreasonable. If more than a thousand telegraph offices were completely closed, more than a thousand wireless stations would have to be established to replace them. Not only does that not conform to economic principles, I am afraid that it is not allowed by facts either! It can be seen that wired telegraphs still need to be reorganized. Recently, I heard that the telecommunications authorities are doing their best to reorganize wired electricity. In terms of equipment, such as repairing lines and purchasing the latest machines, to ensure accuracy and speed. In terms of business, such as making fees low, and increasing the number of telegraph offices and postal and telecommunications agencies in major cities and towns and railway stations, all facilities are for the sake of promoting business and facilitating the people. It is considered a satisfactory thing!

㈡ Wireless Telegraph My country has a vast territory, and transportation in remote provinces is inconvenient. It is indeed quite difficult to build wired telegraphs. Because wireless electricity does not require the erection of lines, it does not have any difficulty setting up wireless stations in remote provinces and regions, even if there are high mountains and ridges. Wireless electricity has a considerable effect on remote communication. In the future, we should try our best to add remote radio stations. Not only will the people in remote areas get the convenience of communication, but it will also have a great effect on national defense. Secondly, my country's international telecommunications traffic has always relied on foreign merchants' water line companies to handle it, and it is inevitably restricted everywhere. Since the establishment of the International Radio Station, international communications have of course received considerable results, saving more than three million yuan in lost profits every year. It can be seen that wireless telegraphs have to be developed as much as possible in remote provinces and regions, and internationally.

㈢ Wired Telephone Wired telephone has the distinction of long-distance telephone and city telephone. Long-distance telephone is divided into two types: ministry-run and province-run, and city telephone also has two types: ministry-run and commercial-run. Recently, the development of long-distance telephone operated by provinces has been quite rapid, which inevitably affects the telegraph business. However, both telegraph and telephone are sharp tools for communication. Of course, it cannot be said that there is no need for long-distance telephone if there is a telegraph. However, for the sake of facilitating the people and conforming to economic principles, it seems that the long-distance telephone operated by the provinces does not need to set up lines in parallel with the long-distance telephone lines operated by the ministry, so as to avoid mutual competition and both sides being hurt. I remember that President Wang once said in his inaugural speech at the Ministry of Communications Telecommunications Conference that state-owned enterprises should work together. Then, the provincial long-distance telephone should first develop as much as possible in places where there is no long-distance telephone operated by the ministry, connecting calls, and connecting and transferring reports and calls with the long-distance telephone operated by the ministry and the telegraph bureau, so that the people can get real communication convenience.

Regarding city telephones, such as the recovery of the Shanghai Concession telephone issue and the improvement of machinery in various bureaus, they are all urgent plans to be drawn up. As for the telephone business, special attention must be paid to reforming bad habits and cracking down on arrears. In addition, the switchboard operators should be polite and courteous to users, and the connection should be as quick as possible, so that users are satisfied and the business can be developed.

㈣ Broadcasting Radio Station In recent years, the people of Shanghai and other major cities have been very interested in installing wireless radio receivers. Therefore, the private broadcasting stations in Shanghai have also adapted to the needs and have been increasing day by day. Among them, there are inevitably a small number of broadcasting stations that covet petty profits and secretly contact foreign firms, using wireless electricity to report commercial market conditions, which have been discovered and cracked down on by the inspection radio station of the International Telecommunications Bureau. Therefore, the development of wireless telephone, although it is a good phenomenon, it must also have considerable sanctions. If broadcasting stations can be allowed to report commercial market conditions concurrently, that will interfere with the business of the state-run telegraph bureau. I hope that the supervisors of telegraph bureaus in various places pay attention to this point, which may have something to do with the development of business.

Finally, my country's telegraph bureaus have always paid too little attention to publicity. It is rare to see business advertisements published by telegraph bureaus in various newspapers and magazines, so that the general public's impression of telegrams is very weak, which is also a reason why the telegraph business cannot develop. "Telegraph commercialization" is the proposition of the telecommunications authorities over the years. Advertising is a sharp tool for commercial publicity. This business advertising item must be paid more attention to, and it will always have considerable returns. I hope that the telecommunications authorities will promote telecommunications, especially international telecommunications, to a greater extent, so that everyone understands that international radio stations are sharp tools for promoting domestic products and saving profits. Then the future development of telecommunications will be unlimited!

Talk About Telephones (II) 294

— Ji Ran

In the essay in issue 22 of this publication, I stated that shared-battery telephone systems have their advantages, so even with the rise of automatic systems, shared-battery systems have not been eliminated. The advantage of the so-called shared-battery system is that if the management is good and the connection is fast, it is no different from an automatic telephone. However, the shared-battery system requires switchboard operators, and the services that these switchboard operators can provide to the public are often very useful. Mechanical automation can only bring more benefits to drivers. This is also one of the reasons why the shared-battery system is praised.

In 1927, an incident at the Shanghai Nanshi Telephone Bureau was often talked about. It was in the autumn, but I forgot the exact night. A child in a family in Nanshi was suffering from a serious illness, and they called various doctors in the city by telephone, but no one responded after midnight. At this time, the Shanghai bureau's telephone was a shared-battery system. Since there was no way to call a doctor, they told the switchboard operator and asked if there was any way to get a doctor from the concession to come. When asked which doctor they wanted, they said that they could choose either so-and-so or so-and-so. The switchboard operator, because it was midnight and the switchboard was not busy, successively called on their behalf. As a result, a doctor actually came to the door, and the child's illness was saved. Several days later, the child's parents went to the telephone bureau in person to ask who was on duty at the time, thanked them in person, and then placed an advertisement in the newspaper to thank them.

With automatic telephones, there is no switchboard operator to make the connection. The occurrence of this kind of accidental event is due to the operator. An operator is not necessary, but sometimes an operator can help the user, making the user fully satisfied. The following sections, translated from Western magazines, are also credible and have evidence!

When a fire occurs, users are often flustered and confused, and they often make mistakes when dialing the number, so that the fire department, police station, or insurance company they are calling cannot be reached for a while. If you use a shared-battery telephone, you only need to pick up the receiver and say the word "fire," and the operator will quickly transfer the call. In fact, it is much easier than using an automatic telephone. This is what some American users have experienced, and it is also why they recommend shared-battery telephones.

Theft also inevitably occurs in major American cities. For prevention, the important telephones of major companies are all installed underground, and a secret telephone is often installed separately in case of accidents. This kind of secret telephone is also suitable for shared-battery systems, because in the event of a robbery, you only need to have the telephone in hand and say the word "thief" lightly to the operator, without having to turn the dial and reveal your voice.

The rest are for social welfare matters. For private emergencies, being served by an operator on the telephone has more benefits than calling directly with an automatic telephone, and it cannot be denied across the board. (End)

Attention to Those Installing Broadcasting Radio Receivers 295

— Di You

Jin Huanyan Did Not Apply to Register a Privately Installed Radio Receiver

Tianjin Radio Station Detained and Sent to Court, Sentenced to a Fine

Jin Huanyan (also known as Jin Huanran and Jin Zhao Zhi) used to work in the wireless industry and has some electrical knowledge. Recently, he opened the Tianjin Xinyi Bank with others and engaged in the gold business. On November 29 of last year, he purchased two wireless radio receivers one after another and privately installed them at home (No. 29, Gongyi Lane, British Concession, Tianjin) to listen to the gold price market conditions issued by private radio stations for the use of the bank. The matter was detected by the Tianjin Radio Station on the 2nd of this month, and it reported to the Public Security Bureau of the Provincial Capital of Hebei Province, which went to search with the British Engineering Bureau. The case was solved on the spot, and the witnesses were transferred to the Tianjin District Court for trial. After being prosecuted by the procuratorate of the court according to law and after repeated trials, Jin Huanyan was finally sentenced to a fine of 1,200 yuan because he had not applied to register a privately installed radio receiver, which violated the provisions of Article 3 of the Telecommunications Regulations, in accordance with the provisions of Article 21 of the regulations.

The Provisional Measures for the Registration of Broadcasting Radio Receivers have long been promulgated by the Ministry of Communications. All those who install radio receivers should apply to the radio stations under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Communications in various places in accordance with the regulations and obtain a registration certificate before they are legal. Article 9 of the registration measures also stipulates: "If a household receives any radio signals other than broadcasting radio from its radio receiver, it shall keep it confidential." Now that Jin Huanyan has neither applied for registration nor listened to the gold price market conditions issued by the illegal private radio stations for profit, he has clearly violated the provisions of Article 3 of the Telecommunications Regulations and Article 9 of the Provisional Measures for the Registration of Radio Receivers. Now he has been sentenced to a fine of 1,200 yuan, which is entirely his own fault and deserves it. However, the circumstances of this case are different from the previous case of Yongli Bank and other private radio stations: Jin Huanyan only installed two radio receivers and did not have a transmitter, so he could not disturb the radio signals sent by others, and he himself could not send reports. Therefore, the damage to the national telecommunications business is small. Weighing the pros and cons, it cannot be compared with the Yongli Bank case and convicted of theft.

I have a feeling about this: All countries have regulations for the management of broadcasting radio receivers, and registration fees must be collected. People who install radio receivers all abide by laws and regulations and register in accordance with the registration procedures, which fully demonstrates that they are orderly and organized countries. However, my country is not like that. People often disregard national laws and regulations. Taking the registration of radio receivers as an example, it is enough to prove the superficiality of our legal concepts. According to surveys, there are about hundreds of thousands of households in the country that have installed radio receivers, but those who comply with the order to apply for registration are very few. Most of these hundreds of thousands of radio receiver installers are knowledgeable people with better living conditions, but they despise laws and regulations so much, which is really a manifestation of our people's lack of civic training. It is enough to expose the inferior roots of our nation and provide outsiders with ridicule. I heard that the communications authorities will set a deadline to order all telecommunications agencies under their jurisdiction to strictly crack down on unregistered radio receivers. I sincerely hope that all installers will quickly register automatically and not delay any longer, so as not to be punished by law and bring trouble to themselves!

The registration of radio receivers does not require any fees, and the procedures are very simple. The registration procedures are excerpted below for the reference of all radio receiver installers:

㈠ Each installer may obtain a registration application form from any of the following telecommunications agencies under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Communications, and shall fill in all the items in the application in detail: Shanghai, Nanjing, Beijing, Tianjin, Hankou, Ningbo, Wuhu Telegraph Bureau, Fuzhou, Dinghai, Xiamen, Chongming, Qidong, Shantou, Yichang, Nanchang, Changsha, Guangzhou, Qingdao, Jinan, Yantai, Ba County, Chengdu, Wanxian, Chang'an (Xi'an), Ningbo, Guiyang, Lanzhou,

㈡ The registrant shall fill in the following items in the registration application form: (A) Type of machine parts; (B) Antenna style; (C) Current supply status; (D) Wavelength range; (E) Machine value.

㈢ If there are any inaccuracies in the registration application form filled in by each installer, once discovered, it shall be treated as unregistered, and a corresponding fine shall be imposed in accordance with the provisions of Article 21 of the Telecommunications Regulations.

World Telecommunications 296

— Reporter

Germany's Opening of Daytime Picture Telegraphs

According to German newspaper reports: Daytime picture transmission has now been extended to the public to transmit photos, such as wedding photos and birthday photos. Group photos or landscape photos taken with a fast lens can also be entrusted to telecommunication. This is regarded as a beautiful telegram. German postal and telecommunications bureaus all receive these daytime picture telegrams. The price of a daytime picture of 100 square centimeters is only four marks (approximately US$1.50) domestically.

The Popularity of Interpersonal Telegrams in Czechoslovakia

Since May 1, Czech telegraph bureaus have begun to receive a type of inexpensive telegram with beautiful envelopes that can be used for birthday and anniversary celebrations. A total of 8,000 of these telegrams were received in May, showing their widespread use.

The Expansion of Long-Distance Telephone in the Philippines

The Philippine Long Distance Telephone Company plans to connect Manila with Tokyo, Hong Kong, and Shanghai this year. This plan is part of its operation of global overseas wireless telephone services. The construction of the Manila-Hong Kong circuit may be completed before the Manila-Tokyo circuit, because the Hong Kong authorities have already promised to connect their local organizations and are now engaged in the necessary facilities. The Rapid Progress of Telecommunications in Soviet Russia

The first automatic telephone trunk line between Moscow and Bershin (approximately 625 miles) has recently been opened for business. The third automatic telephone exchange, which can accommodate 4,000 households, has also recently been opened in Moscow. The direct telegraph line between Moscow and Vladivostok has been completed. This line, which is approximately 6,000 miles long, will completely avoid the delays of previous intermediate bureau transmissions. In addition, a direct telephone line between London and Leningrad has also been established.

Parisian Travelogue 297

— Zou Mao Tong

On October 9, at 11:15 pm, we left Geneva. We were in a third-class carriage, which was originally supposed to hold eight people per compartment, but there were only four of us in the same compartment, so we could barely sleep at night. The seats were all leather cushions, which were no less comfortable than the second-class carriages in my country. We arrived in Paris at 8:15 am on the 10th.

We stayed in Paris for a relatively long time. We visited the French Wireless Radio Factory (SFR for short), the commercially-run Radio France station, and the engineering laboratory of the Standard Electric Company.

The scale of the wireless radio factory is not large, about the same as the electrical manufacturing factory of the Construction Committee. It is divided into metal hardware and transceiver manufacturing departments. When we went to visit, we saw that most of the machines made inside were used on airplanes, warships, and merchant ships. They also make broadcast radios, the largest of which has a power of I2okw. There are also mobile radio stations for the air force. The transceivers are installed on two cars and can be driven to any location to communicate with the aircraft, which is also a powerful tool for modern military transportation.

Commercial wireless radio is partly state-run and is located in the post office. The locations it communicates with are limited to French colonies and some European countries, such as Russia and Persia. The rest are handled by the commercially-run wireless radio station. It is said that the station was established very early, and the French government granted it patent rights at that time. Its transmitting and receiving stations are all located outside the city, while the central receiving and transmitting room is located in the city. There are seven iokw shortwave transmitters, only one of which is a crystal type, and the rest are active oscillation high-power amplification type (M.O.P.A.). There are also eight high-frequency AC longwave machines with power ranging from 500kw to 25kw. The shortwave machines are used to communicate with the United States, China, Japan, and South America, while the longwave machines are used to work with European countries. The equipment at the receiving station is mostly old, but there is one relatively new one that was purchased from Marconi Company. The telegrams at the central receiving and transmitting room are all transferred from the General Post Office and have no direct receiving rights. In addition to telegrams transmitted by telephone, the post office also delivers them. The transmission between the post office and the receiving and transmitting room is aided by vacuum tubes, so there is no delay in incoming and outgoing telegrams. Outgoing telegrams are transmitted from the post office to the receiving and transmitting room through vacuum tubes, and then directly sent to the reporter's workstation through vacuum tubes. There are a total of fourteen communication locations, among which there are three in East Asia: Shanghai, Shenyang, and Tokyo. London is the busiest in terms of report affairs, with about 2,000 incoming and outgoing reports every day. Three machines are used simultaneously when busy. The fatigue length used between London and Paris is 2200 meters to 900 meters. New York telegrams were also very busy, but now that an agreement has been established with the Water Line Company, most of the telegrams are sent by the Water Line. The receiving and transmitting machines of the Water Line Company are also located in the room and work with New York at the same time. Overall, the equipment of the station, except for the use of vacuum tubes to transmit incoming and outgoing telegrams, and the layout of the receiving and transmitting room, seem to be far inferior to my international radio station and not worth mentioning.

The research laboratory of the Standard Electric Company is located in Paris, and its main factory is in London. Whenever there is a new invention in engineering, the research laboratory first makes a model and then hands it over to the main factory in London for manufacturing. The current work of the research laboratory, in terms of wireless radio, is the ultra-short wave (Ultra Short Wamve) and the Micro Ray experiment, and the manufacture of light bulbs above 50kw. It is said that the test room has used I8cm to test the telegram with London. The test has been carried out for several months, and the results are very good. The method is to set up two i8cm radio stations at a distance of about thirty miles, and then transfer them separately through landlines to London and Paris. The room is also planning a new type of wireless radio typewriter (Radio Jeleprinaer). Each English letter is composed of points generated by seven different wavelengths. The one we saw was the second model made by the company, and it will soon be seen in practical use. As for transmitting light bulbs, those below 50kw are manufactured in London, and those that are particularly large are manufactured in Paris. The light bulbs with the largest power can reach 300kw.

Explanation of Telegraph Terminology 298

— Qinghua

In the manuscripts published in this journal and the various telegraph business regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Communications, there are often telegraph business terms. To make it easier for readers to understand, the most commonly used terms are annotated below:

Sending Bureau: The telegraph bureau that sends the telegram. The place name written in the "Name of Sending Bureau" column at the top of the incoming telegram form is the name of the sending bureau.

Receiving Bureau: The telegraph bureau that delivers the telegram.

Transmitting Bureau: The intermediate telegraph bureau that relays the telegram.

Sender: The person who sends the telegram. Whether it is a private business, a firm, or an organization, all are referred to as the sender.

Recipient: The person who receives the telegram.

Payment Indication: In addition to ordinary, urgent, and news telegrams, there are various special delivery methods that can be used. For example, to avoid transmission errors, the telegraph bureau can be asked to proofread the telegram during transmission. Such telegrams should be marked with "TC." If a reply fee is prepaid, the telegram is marked with "RP······." These marks are called payment indications.

Payment Official Telegram: If the recipient has questions after receiving the telegram, they can send a payment official telegram, which is more cost-effective than sending an ordinary telegram to inquire. (Starting this year, for the convenience of the public, the Ministry of Communications has specially approved free inquiries for telegrams with doubtful content. However, inquiries about the sender's name, etc., are still subject to fees.) If the sender needs to correct, supplement, or cancel a telegram that has already been sent, they can also send a payment official telegram.

Bureau Station: A simplified term for telegraph bureaus and wireless radio stations.

Telegram: A simplified term for telegram. For example, "outgoing telegram" refers to a telegram that has been sent, and "incoming telegram" refers to a telegram that has been received. The telegraph bureau does not use the character "電" (diàn, electricity) but uses the character "報" (bào, report) as a simplification of "電報" (diànbào, telegram) to distinguish it from "電話" (diànhuà, telephone), as the simplification of "電話" is "話" (huà, speech) instead of "電." Furthermore, business places that also handle telephone services are abbreviated as "報話營業處" (bàohuà yíngyèchù, telegraph and telephone business offices), which is more appropriate than using the character "電." (To be continued)

Bi-Weekly News 299

— Associate

Strict Inspection of the Business of Various Receiving and Sending Offices

Previously, in order to facilitate the public, the Ministry of Communications specially established many receiving and sending offices in major commercial ports. These receiving and sending offices are generally far from the central bureau. Whether the staff in these offices are dedicated to their duties, whether they strictly adhere to business hours, whether they treat the public who send telegrams with courtesy, and whether they calculate change for telegram fees according to the announced rates all require regular inspection to facilitate business. The Ministry of Communications has now specifically formulated a "Methods for Inspecting Telegraph Bureau Receiving and Sending Offices" and ordered all telegraph bureaus to comply with it. It is expected that all receiving and sending offices will provide services as thorough as the central bureau, to benefit the public.

Official Military Telegram Paper Must Be Signed by the Supervising Officer

Previously, the Ministry of Communications found that official military telegrams from various telegraph bureaus were rampant, which not only hindered the rapid transmission of commercial telegrams but also often delayed important official military telegrams. It was specifically stipulated that, in the future, when personnel from various agencies send official military telegrams on business trips, the supervising officer must first sign or stamp the telegram paper in advance to show caution and avoid redundancy. The Ministry of Communications has submitted this measure to the Executive Yuan for forwarding to the National Government for promulgation to all political and military agencies, to be implemented starting in January of next year.

Revising the Calculation Standard for Long-Distance Telephone Rates

Recently, the Ministry of Communications has actively constructed long-distance telephone lines in various places, and the business has developed rapidly. Currently, the old long-distance telephone rates are mostly based on line length, so the rates between two places that are very close in distance are often very high because the lines are not direct but circuitous. In recent years, the construction of highways in various provinces has been rapidly advancing, and the original rates are mostly unsuitable. In order to make fees fair and to develop telephone services, the Ministry of Communications has decided to reorganize long-distance telephone rates, using spatial distance as the standard, and to limit the duration of each call to three minutes. The Beijing-Baoding, Tianjin-Jinan-Yushulin, Tianjin-Jinan, Jinan-Qingdao, Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou lines and the telephone lines in Jiangxi and Fujian provinces will be implemented first. The specific implementation date will be announced after the rates have been finalized.
